Important News

Ma Zhanshan's Troops Advance to Hu-Hai Railway 79

Jilin Troops Concentrated Under Ma's Orders

Japanese Troops Dig Trenches at Songpu Station

Hu-Hai Vehicles Taken by Ma

Harbin Correspondence - The Hu-Hai Railway has been blocked since April 28th. Residents along the railway line have been moving to Harbin in recent days. Merchants and residents of Songpu Town, separated from Harbin City by a river, have also moved away, and all houses are nailed shut. Employees and road workers at Majiachuan Station on the Hu-Hai Railway and Songpu Station mostly hide elsewhere at night and only go to the station during the day to check. Gao Yunkun, the former General Manager of the Hu-Hai Railway Bureau, took leave to go to Fula Erji due to his mother's illness. The puppet state's Ministry of Transportation reassigned Chang Zunyi to take over. Chang is the younger brother of Chang Bingyi, the current Director of the Shanxi Agriculture and Mining Department. He obtained this position through contact with the Japanese. He originally planned to take over on the 29th, but did not dare to go to the bureau due to the disruption of transportation. The affairs of the Hu-Hai Railway Bureau at Songpu Station are currently temporarily maintained by the original Director of the General Affairs Department, Dou. However, most of the employees have gone to Hailun, and there is nothing to do. It is just a nominal position. On the morning of the 29th, two groups of Japanese troops got off the train from the Miaotaizi Station on the Chinese Eastern Railway and went to Songpu Station. The first group, about one company, dug trenches near the East Factory of the station. The second group, transferred from the Harbin-Suifenhe Railway, consisted of about 2,000 people and planned to go to Hulan by train. Because Songpu Station only had 15 freight cars and no locomotives, they did not go and stayed at the station. This traffic interruption was unexpected by the Japanese. Ma Zhanshan's troops, the Cai Hongyou Brigade, arrived in Suihua from eastern Heilongjiang under Ma's orders. On the morning of the 28th, the Lu Tuan of the brigade also led a battalion of soldiers and drove a special train to Songpu Station. They immediately showed Ma's order to mobilize employees to Hailun to work to maintain the property of the Hu-Hai Railway. All locomotives and freight cars were completely driven to Hailun. The Railway Bureau also moved to Hailun. Employees who were willing to go would go, otherwise they would be suspended. At that time, the employees heard that 19 were willing to go with the army. The passenger and freight vehicles parked at the station were completely coupled into a train, which departed for Hulan at about 10:00 AM. Before the train departed, a stationmaster refused to issue a road permit because he had not received an order from the director, and was immediately shot by the Lu Tuan. By noon, there was no one left in the Hu-Hai Railway Bureau. At that time, the Japanese troops in Harbin heard the news and were about to cross the river to pursue, but the telegraphic communication between the north and south of the river was cut off by the Lu Tuan in advance, and the situation there was unknown. The Japanese troops did not dare to rush in. On the morning of the 29th, the Japanese troops finally learned the truth and feared that Ma's troops would attack and enter Harbin. They hurriedly sent troops to Songpu to set up defenses. On the morning of the 29th at 5:00 AM, a passenger train departed from the Hulan Bureau and drove to Majiachuan Station. When they heard that the Japanese troops were crossing the river, they returned to Hulan without stopping. In the afternoon, traffic between Hulan and Songpu, except for trains, was not available even by horse-drawn carriage. Harbin merchants were extremely panicked and closed the market early. The Xi Qia military police Second Brigade, Li Wenbing's unit, stationed in Harbin, and the Japanese troops deployed defenses in the suburbs of Harbin, including Yuanjia Wopeng, Huangshan Zuzi, and Sanke Shu. The situation was extremely tense. Currently, the vanguard of Ma's troops, the Cai Hongyou Brigade, is at Xujia Station and Zhangshiyingdian on the Hu-Hai Railway, 20 miles away from the vanguard of the Japanese troops at Songpu Station. Both sides are taking defensive positions and have not yet engaged in fighting. Traffic between Hulan and Hailun is still normal for freight and passenger cars. The workers transferred from Songpu are all gathered in Hulan to serve. Recently, the Hei troops Wu Songlin and Pu Datong have been ordered by Ma to concentrate in Keshan and Baiquan. At the same time, the passenger and freight cars on the Qiqihar Railway were also reportedly mobilized by Ma's team to Taian Town on the 28th. The Tahar Railway Bridge has been blown up. The Japanese Amano Brigade stationed in Heilongjiang is defending the Longjiang Station on the Qiqihar line outside the city. The Japanese troops seem to be planning to wait for the arrival of the new 8th and 9th Divisions before launching an attack on Ma's troops. Ma has recently been making great efforts to recruit various rebel forces and has also ordered the local militias to concentrate in Baiquan, Wangkui, and Hailun to await orders. The rebel force of Li Qingshan, which was dispatched from Harbin for a long time, has also been reorganized by Ma into the 4th Infantry Regiment and the 2nd Cavalry Regiment, which are currently being organized in Shitouchengzi. In the future, it is still planned to dispatch troops to Nongan and Changchun to remotely control the Japanese troops coming from the north. (April 29th)

After the Ministry of Foreign Affairs investigated the evidence, it immediately lodged a serious protest. In view of such actions, we consider them to be extremely illegal. Therefore, our country, in order to eliminate such worries, should take decisive measures.

Commemoration of the May Third Incident in Jinan 83

Amidst Bitter Winds and Rain

Doubly Presenting a Tragic Atmosphere

Jinan Correspondence: Time flies, and years pass like flowing water. Today marks the fourth anniversary of the May Third Massacre. The people of Jinan, having personally experienced the devastation of artillery fire, hold a particularly solemn memorial service every year on this day to show they will never forget. On this day, the entire city flies flags at half-mast to express grief. All schools hold memorial meetings. Schools above the secondary level suspend classes for one day. Various newspapers publish special editions, featuring photos of the May Third Massacre. The Provincial Party Headquarters prints commemorative booklets of the May Third Massacre, along with letters to compatriots and comrades, to arouse the attention of all sectors. It also convenes representatives from all sectors in the Party Headquarters auditorium to hold a memorial meeting. At the time, the sky is gloomy and overcast, with a fine drizzle. The whole of Jinan presents a tragic atmosphere. More than a thousand representatives from all sectors arrive. In the center of the auditorium are placed the memorial tablets of Martyr Cai Gongshi and the comrades who died in the May Third Incident. The meeting place is also silent and without sound, very different from ordinary meetings. The chairman is Zhang Weicun, the Provincial Rectification Committee member. After opening the meeting as scheduled, the entire assembly bows three times to the memorial tablets of the martyrs who died in the May Third Incident. Then Zhang Weicun reports on the purpose of the meeting, briefly stating that today is the fourth anniversary of the May Third Massacre. However, in the four years since, internal strife has not ceased, and the revenge for the May Third Incident has not been taken. The tragedies of the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident have followed one after another. As of now, the severity of the domestic situation is unprecedented in history. He hopes that everyone will unite to wash away the national shame, and especially hopes that young students will cultivate their knowledge to serve the country in the future. Then representatives give speeches, and finally disperse after shouting slogans. (May 3rd)

Alarming News from Northern Guangdong 84

Chen and Zhao's Troops Mutiny in Pingshi

Li Mingrui's Forces Suddenly Invade Renhua

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since the loss of Zhangzhou and Quanzhou in Fujian, the Guangdong army has planned to transfer the Third Army under Li Yangjing, the First Independent Division under Huang Renyu, the Second Independent Division under Zhang Ruigui, and parts of the Fourth and Fifth Divisions of the Second Army, to defend the Fujian-Guangdong border. These troops are deployed in a long, snaking line stretching north from Sannan on the Jiangxi border, winding through Xunwu, Jiaoling, Lianping, Heping, Pingyuan, Dabu, and Meixian, maintaining close vigilance while temporarily holding their positions to await an opportunity before making further advances. Consequently, Yu Hanmou, the overall commander of the aid to Jiangxi, is currently stationed in Ganzhou, and Li Yangjing, the overall commander of the aid to Fujian, remains in Dabu. However, as the majority of the Guangdong army has advanced to southern Jiangxi and the Fujian border, the defenses of the Northern and Eastern Rivers have been somewhat relaxed, allowing miscellaneous troops and local communists to take advantage of the situation. Recently, Chen Tiejian and Zhao Zixin from southern Hunan suddenly rebelled in the name of demanding supplies, occupying Pingshi and Lechang in the Northern River to restrain the Guangdong army entering southern Jiangxi. It is known that Chen and Zhao's brigades were recruited by Tang Shengzhi when the Southwest Extraordinary Conference was held. Not long after, Tang left, and Chen and Zhao's troops were reorganized under Chen Jitang's First Army Group, with Pingshi and Yizhang designated as the defense areas for the two brigades. Recently, for unknown reasons, a mutiny suddenly occurred, with signs of invading Renhua and Lechang. The Guangdong authorities immediately transferred He Baoshu's Second Regiment of Chen Hanguang's brigade, stationed in the Northern River, from Shaoguan to Pingshi to intercept the rebels. On April 27th, they engaged in a fierce battle with the rebel soldiers. To increase its forces, Chen's brigade redeployed Chen Yuguang's First Regiment to Lechang to assist in the suppression, and dispatched Peng Zhifang's Third Regiment from Xiaobeijiang to Lianxian to cut off the enemy's rear. After arriving in Lianxian, Peng's troops, together with Li Kangxiu's Third Regiment of Chen Zhang's Second Independent Brigade, went straight to Xingzi to intercept Zhao Zixin and Gong Hao's forces. Chen Hanguang returned to Lechang from Shaoguan on the 28th to command the operation. By the end of last month, the rebel soldiers in Pingshi were driven back. Unexpectedly, more than two thousand of these rebel soldiers retreated to southern Hunan and joined forces with Li Mingrui's communist bandit forces from southern Jiangxi, launching a surprise attack on Renhua County from Guidong and other places in southern Hunan. Earlier, on the 24th, about a thousand local communists had gathered within Renhua County, occupying Changjiangwei in Renhua County. Changjiangwei is located between Nanxiong and Renhua, and the situation is quite tense. Yuan's battalion of the defense army stationed in Renhua dispatched two companies of soldiers to suppress them. By this time, the bandit forces had already occupied Muxitou, Zhou Cave, and other places. When the government troops arrived, they engaged the bandits, but due to their weak forces, they were defeated and retreated. With the loss of Changjiangwei, Renhua County was shaken and repeatedly sent urgent reports. Chen Zhang's Second Independent Brigade stationed in Nanxiong redeployed Du Fengfei's regiment to encircle and suppress the bandits. However, Du's regiment suffered more than a hundred casualties, including over ten platoon leaders and six or seven company commanders, and still failed. Currently, the province is redeploying Luo Cequn's First Regiment of Miao Peinan's Training Division, which arrived in Shaoguan on the 30th to strengthen the defense, so that Chen Hanguang's troops can be transferred from Shaozhou and Lechang to Renhua to suppress Li's bandits. Currently, the bandit forces have spread from Changjiangwei to Chengkou, and Renhua County is under pressure from both directions. Merchants and residents in the area are fleeing in droves. It is reported that He's regiment of Chen's brigade and a part of the First Regiment had arrived in Renhua on the 28th, dividing into several routes to encircle and suppress the bandits in Chengkou and Changjiang. (May 3rd)

Opening of the Jiangxi Province Bandit Suppression Conference 85

Xiong Shihui Delivers Opening Remarks

Strongly Criticizing the Jiangxi People for Being Too Useless

Nanchang Correspondence: Since the 16th year of the Republic of China, communist bandits have spread in Jiangxi, now almost all over the province. To understand the details of communist bandits in various places, so that military, political, financial construction, and relief efforts can develop a comprehensive and precise suppression plan, the provincial government convened a bandit suppression conference. A total of 120 representatives were publicly elected from 81 counties, and the provincial government invited more than 40 people, including Li Liejun, Zhang Dingfan, Tang Yi, Xie Yuanhan, Kong Shaoyao, and Zhou Guanhong. More than 180 proposals and more than 40 county bandit suppression reports have been received and included in the agenda. The meeting is scheduled to last ten days, and the opening ceremony will be held on May 4th in the auditorium of the Provincial Party Headquarters. 119 members including Kong Shaoyao and Jiang Dajie attended the meeting, and more than 100 guests including He Yingqin, Minister of Military and Political Affairs, attended. All members of the provincial government, directors of various departments, the president of the High Court, and the director of the Highway Administration were also present. The meeting opened at around 10 a.m., chaired by Xiong Shihui. After the ceremony, Xiong Shihui delivered an opening speech, stating that in the past six or seven years, communist bandits have burned, killed, robbed, and plundered in Jiangxi, affecting as many as 70 of the 81 counties. The loss of life and property of the people is incalculable. The reason why the situation has reached such an incurable point is not, as outsiders say, how formidable Zhu and Mao are, or that the bandits have three heads and six arms, but that the people of Jiangxi themselves are not formidable enough and are too useless. Even the current atmosphere of terror, as if it were a big deal, is created by corrupt troops, greedy officials, and scholars who are neither one thing nor another. When corrupt troops arrive at the front, they retreat without fighting and flee at the mere sight of the enemy, claiming how formidable the bandits are and how amazing Zhu and Mao are, to cover up their crime of not fighting, being afraid of death, and being useless. Greedy officials scrape the land bare and then hope for the bandits to come, so that they can falsely report losses and run away with the money. Scholars who are neither one thing nor another say how Zhu and Mao understand doctrine and how they gain the support of the people. In fact, Zhu and Mao are both uneducated and unskilled, and not qualified to talk about doctrine. The target of communism is big capital. To talk about communism in China today is like wearing fur in summer and linen in winter. Therefore, the current atmosphere of everyone being seen as a soldier is all due to mediocre people disturbing themselves and lacking the determination to save themselves. Local officials, gentry, and even ordinary people in the province all have a mentality of following the old ways, being negligent, relying on others, and being biased, which has led to the communist bandits becoming strong and out of control. Instead of blaming themselves for being useless, they elevate the bandits too high, which is truly heartbreaking. Therefore, in the future, we must eliminate all the previous atmosphere of decadence and laziness, and rise up together to save ourselves. Even dozens of Zhu and Mao are not to be feared. Then He Yingqin gave instructions, briefly stating that when the large-scale suppression of bandits was carried out last year, it was originally hoped that all the bandits could be eliminated. However, due to the influence of the situation, inconvenient transportation, poor local politics, and the people being like a heap of loose sand, the communist bandits were able to rise from the ashes, which is truly regrettable. However, after Zhu and Mao suffered a major defeat in Xingguo last year, they advocated fleeing to Hunan and Fujian, and opinions were divided. In addition, lower-level cadres from the Jiangxi and Hunan factions killed each other, and the number of those who came to surrender with their weapons increased day by day. Recently, in the battle of Ganzhou, the remaining communist bandits were severely damaged again, and they fled in three directions: one to southern Fujian, one to the Hunan-Guangdong border, and one to remain in the old nest in southeastern Jiangxi. This time, when Guangdong and Guangxi sent troops, Comrades Li Delin and Chen Bonan both wanted me to take on the task of commander-in-chief of the three provinces' bandit suppression, and the command is unified. In the past, the bandit suppression troops were affected by the situation, and their efforts fell short. Now, the Southwest is extremely supportive of the central government. When I was in Luoyang, I heard that Comrade Yan Baichuan also earnestly admonished his subordinate generals to unite in suppressing bandits and resisting Japan, and to point their guns outward. Therefore, at this moment, we can concentrate on suppressing bandits and will no longer be affected by the overall situation. However, relying solely on the army to suppress bandits is not effective, and suppressing small groups still requires party affairs and politics. What should be noted in the future is (1) improving politics to eliminate the source of bandits, (2) improving transportation to benefit the army and develop production, and (3) organizing the people to enable them to defend themselves, with the basic work being to check household registration and manage the baojia system. For example, the reason why Peng's bandits did not dare to enter southern Hunan when they fled into Rucheng this time was due to the power of the local militias. In addition, regarding military matters, it is not convenient to announce. What can be announced is that in the future, the areas where bandits are active will be divided into several zones, and each zone will be the responsibility of one person to suppress and eliminate them within a time limit, to avoid shirking responsibility. Then Wang Guanying delivered a speech on behalf of the Provincial Party Headquarters, and Wu Zongci delivered a reply on behalf of the members. The meeting adjourned at 12 noon. (April 5th)

Chen Diaoyuan Suppresses Bandits in Anhui 86

Wuhu Correspondence: The bandit problem in western Anhui has been spreading more and more widely recently. After Chen Diaoyuan stepped down from his post in Anhui, the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs ordered Chen to handle the bandit suppression affairs in Anhui, with specific responsibilities. After receiving the order, Chen moved the headquarters from Anqing to Bengbu and went to Hefei to supervise the suppression. Currently, the bandit suppression troops include the 46th Division of Yue Shengxuan, the 55th Division of Ruan Zhaochang, the 57th Division of Li Songshan, the 7th Division of Wang Jun, the 12th Division of Zeng Wanzhong, and several aircraft. The intensity of the bandit suppression war can be imagined. Zhejiang People Rise Up in Opposition to Tax Increases 87

Hangzhou News: The Zhejiang Provincial Government has decided to increase the business tax rate from 2/1000 to 10/1000, ordering the various business tax collection bureaus under the Finance Department to comply. However, the tax payments for the spring term will still be collected according to the original tax rate. The revised tax rate is scheduled to be implemented from April onwards. The people of Zhejiang believe that this tax increase is no different from a disguised likin tax. The silk industry in Hangzhou was the first to oppose it, sending telegrams to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministries of Finance and Industry, requesting the Zhejiang Provincial Government to withdraw the order to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. Currently, the new pharmaceutical industry, the electrical machinery industry, the silk weaving industry, and others have successively submitted petitions to the Executive Yuan, requesting that the Zhejiang Provincial Government

Cancel the heavy business tax rate. It is also reported that the Provincial Federation of Commerce also telegraphed the National Government and the Executive Yuan yesterday, stating that commerce, at this critical juncture, cannot bear the heavy tax burden, and requested that the proposal be canceled to save the merchants and people of Zhejiang. On one hand, Wang Zhuzhai of the Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Legislative Yuan to protect the spirit of legislation, requesting that, like the postage increase case, an inquiry be raised to the Executive Yuan. Local News 88

Huayang Bridge Robbery Case: Last night (5th) at around 9 p.m., more than ten bandits speaking a Hakka dialect came to Huayang Bridge in the eastern suburbs of Songjiang County, carrying knives and guns, intending to rob. They first cut off the telephone lines connecting the city and the suburbs, and sent people to guard both the east and west ends. Then, they opened the gate of Zhang Jingen's house, swarmed inside, and searched wantonly. After about a dozen minutes, they took the loot and went down to the countryside, leaving triumphantly. After checking the losses, it was found that gold ornaments, cash, and other items worth about 200 yuan were robbed. The police were immediately notified to investigate and pursue them, but it was too late.

Military Commission Secretly Investigates Accusation: Last month, Jiangyin was ordered to rush to build rear defense projects. Cai Zhongwei, the captain of the Fourth Team of the Engineer Training Department of the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs, led more than ten soldiers to direct the work in Houteng, the second district. Due to a certain issue, Captain Cai took the opportunity to cause trouble. On April 7th, he slapped Shen Xi, the district chief of the district, three times. After mediation, he demanded a reward fee of 200 yuan from the district chief, and the matter was settled. When the matter was heard by a certain director of the Protection Committee Office, he telegraphed Military Commission Chairman Chiang and Executive Yuan President Wang in his capacity as a former subordinate and citizen, requesting a thorough investigation and strict punishment to maintain the reputation of revolutionary soldiers. It is now learned that Chairman Chiang has personally ordered Dai Li, a staff officer of the headquarters, to go to Cheng to investigate secretly. He arrived in Cheng on the 2nd and secretly investigated the truth from all sides. He also went to the brigade headquarters of the Second Brigade of the First Division and summoned County Magistrate Ma Zhen and District Chief Shen Xi to conduct detailed inquiries. It is said that he has gained some clues. Dai left Cheng for Wuxi at noon yesterday (3rd) and returned to Nanjing to report.

Recruiting Female Workers Arouses Repercussions: Wuxi Correspondence: The Ganshen Silk Factory under Gongyun Bridge is operated by Cheng Bingruo from the county. It has a total of twenty-two silk reeling machines. Last year, due to the sluggish silk market and stagnant exports, it was shut down in the winter. Recently, Factory Owner Cheng, in light of the impending resolution of the Sino-Japanese armistice and the improving silk market, originally planned to restart eight machines on the 2nd of this month, but he was very dissatisfied with the old female workers and planned to re-recruit new female workers. The established conditions are: 1. Height should be 4 feet 3 inches. 2. Eyesight should be able to see 16 feet away. 3. The mouth should be toothless and complete. 4. Age should be from 16 to 26 years old. 5. Eloquence should be fluent. 6. Qualifications should be experienced and have worked in factories with complete equipment. 7. The family must not be pregnant or have children. However, there are very few who meet the qualifications. The personnel in charge of the examination in the factory paid particular attention to the female workers' beautiful appearance and fashionable clothing. Female workers with beautiful faces are easily accepted, while those who are slightly ugly have no hope of being qualified. After hearing the news, the old female workers of the factory and the female workers of various factories came out to negotiate and submitted a request to the labor union to forward it to the party and government authorities for relief.

Nanhui Rural Robbers Injure People: The family of Chen Jisheng, a kiln owner in Xiaoguan, about three miles northeast of Nanhui in Jiaxing, was suddenly attacked by two robber boats the night before last. More than twenty robbers broke into the house, tied up and tortured Jisheng, and forced him to hand over his property. Then they tied up and beat his sister and burned her with fire, causing blisters all over her body, which was unbearable to see. The robbers searched and robbed for a long time before leaving triumphantly. Although the injured person was sent to the hospital for treatment, her injuries were quite serious, and there are concerns about her life.

The Shanghai-Hangzhou Provincial Highway to be Completed by a Deadline: Fengxian Correspondence: The Shanghai-Hangzhou Provincial Highway has been planned by the Construction Department. The route is stipulated to start from Shanghai in Jiangsu, with the Shanghai-Minhang Road as the starting point, cross the Huangpu River by the Minhang ferry, pass through the Nanqiao and Nanzhe roads, and then reach Zhapu along the Qinguang Seawall. The Zhejiang section will start from Zhapu along the seawall, cross the Qiantang River bank, and end at Yongjinmen in Hangzhou. It is now learned that, in addition to Fengxian, which has received instructions from the Construction Department yesterday to widen the Nanmin Road by two zhang and to rush to build the Nanzhe Road section to connect, all sections from Zhelintang along the seawall to Zhapu are also being ordered by the department to be completed quickly by Songjiang and Jinshan counties. It is estimated that the entire project will be completed by October of this year at the latest.

Anhui Bandits Rampant and Will Flee into Postal Territory: Gaoyou Correspondence: A large number of bandits from Suyi County in Anhui Province have been entrenched in the Da Ba area, and the blockhouses around Dongyangcheng have been burned down. The situation is extremely serious. Jingou Town in the Twelfth District of the county and Licheng Town in Baoying County are in great danger. It is now heard that Anhui Province will send heavy troops to suppress them, and the bandits will flee into the postal territory.

Zheduo Town Robbed Three Times: (Gaoyou Correspondence:) Zheduo Town in the county has already been robbed twice in April. According to villagers from the area who came to the city, more than a dozen bandits with guns suddenly came on the 29th, searching and robbing every household. In addition to having their clothes, silver, and foreign money robbed, all the rice seeds that had been soaked in water were also looted. It is said that the losses amounted to about seven or eight thousand yuan.

Unlawful Police Captain Sentenced to Ten Years: (Nantong Correspondence:) Yan Diannan, the former police captain of Nantong County, was dismissed and arrested for dereliction of duty and unlawful conduct. He was detained in the Zhenjiang County prison for more than a year. After being tried by a military court, he was sentenced to ten years in prison. The judicial part, such as the case of extorting money from the people, will be tried by the court.

Chen Youren Criticizes the Armistice Agreement 89

Pay Attention to Yoshizawa's Congratulations to Guo Taiqi

Declaring the Return to Normalcy is Not Just Military

Former Foreign Minister Chen Youren made the following comments yesterday on the Sino-Japanese armistice agreement: Is the Sino-Japanese armistice agreement signed on the 5th of this month a victory for China or a victory for Japan? I think the first thing to pay attention to is the following two facts: (1) According to foreign reports, this agreement was originally scheduled to be signed on Monday, May 2nd, but the Japanese requested that it be changed to May 5th. This day is the eleventh anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's establishment of the revolutionary government in Guangzhou. (2) Japanese Foreign Minister Yoshizawa congratulated Vice Minister Guo Taiqi in Tokyo for the signing of this agreement. Naturally, no one would congratulate their enemy on defeating them. These two facts show that the Japanese have recognized that the result of this agreement is a victory for the Japanese. Furthermore, whether we look at the general principles or the detailed clauses of this agreement, I think the Japanese have good reason to recognize this agreement as a symbol of the victory of Japanese policy. Why? Everyone knows that the territory of the Republic of China is completely indivisible. This means that if an enemy invades a part of China (such as Manchuria), it is invading the entire China. That is why the Chinese people insist that the issue of the three northeastern provinces and the issue of Shanghai must be resolved as the same issue. This is the consensus of all Chinese people, and the leader of the Nanjing government, Mr. Wang, has also declared it. But what is the result of this agreement? The Nanjing government and those naive diplomats think that the Shanghai armistice agreement is only a temporary agreement on military issues, and will not involve political issues. Naturally, it will not violate the unity and integrity of the national territory. But is that the case? When a part of country A's territory is invaded by country B, and country A and country B actually sign an agreement for a temporary truce in another part of their territory, while the rest of the territory is still under enemy invasion, isn't this clearly tearing apart the unity and integrity of their own territory? Isn't the so-called "only resolving military issues and not involving politics" just self-deception? There is another level. According to the Lytton Report, the most important point is that it points out that the three northeastern provinces have been in a state of extreme turmoil for seven months since Japan occupied them. The Japanese declaration was originally that the reason they sent troops to occupy the three northeastern provinces was to maintain the治安 of the three northeastern provinces. Now, what can the Japanese say? The League of Nations investigation team has pointed out that the result of the Japanese invasion is only the creation of a state of anarchy in the three northeastern provinces. This is a very bad thing for the Japanese government's international reputation. The Japanese are trying to restore the security of the three northeastern provinces at all costs, even using all the military power of the country, to eliminate the volunteer army of the Chinese people who are resisting Japan to the death, in order to complete their plan to seize the entire three northeastern provinces. On the other hand, we in China have been restricted by this agreement from freely deploying Chinese troops to the surrounding areas of Shanghai, which belongs to our own territory. The Japanese, because they have the guarantee of this agreement, can save the military power of 50,000 troops stationed in Shanghai and huge military expenses. After this, they can hold Shanghai with a small number of troops very comfortably. Isn't this the most beneficial to the Japanese? There is another level. If we examine the clauses of this agreement in detail, such as Article 2, "Before the method of restoring normalcy in the area involved in this agreement has been decided, the Chinese army will remain in its current position." When will the so-called return to normalcy be decided? When will the Japanese agree to the decision? Moreover, the Japanese have also declared that the so-called return to normalcy includes not only military affairs, but also anti-Japanese propaganda and boycotts of Japanese goods. In addition, the Japanese have declared in foreign newspapers that the area they consider to be involved even includes the area south of Suzhou and east of the Huangpu River. However, we have not declared a denial. According to this speculation, is there still hope for our country to restore its sovereignty in Shanghai? Some people may say, "Then do you advocate that it would be better for the Japanese army not to withdraw from Shanghai?" I can answer without a doubt that the Japanese army must withdraw from Shanghai, but not only withdraw from Shanghai, but also withdraw from the three northeastern provinces at the same time. Otherwise, there is only resistance, only desperate resistance.

Shigemitsu's Condition Improves Slightly 90

Extreme Danger Yesterday Noon

Condition Improved in the Evening, Life is Hopeful

After Minister Shigemitsu underwent major surgery to amputate his right leg, he was cared for overnight at Fumin Hospital by famous doctors. After midnight, his body temperature gradually increased, reaching a high of 40 degrees Celsius at 8 a.m. yesterday, which was extremely dangerous. It did not decrease until 1 p.m. After a detailed examination by military medical supervisor and medical doctor Goto, it was determined that it was caused by anemia after surgery.

Blood Transfusion Performed: At 1:30 p.m. yesterday, second-class military doctor Watanabe performed a blood transfusion, taking 300 grams of blood from his brother Shigemitsu's arm and transfusing it to Minister Shigemitsu. However, afterwards, due to the reaction to the blood transfusion, he became more excited, and his body temperature did not decrease.

Condition Improved Last Night: After 2 p.m. yesterday, Dr. Hattori Daisaku of Shinozaki Hospital, together with military medical supervisor Goto, diagnosed and treated him. At 5 p.m., his body temperature gradually decreased. At 6 p.m., his body temperature was 38.2 degrees Celsius, his pulse was 108, and his breathing was 26. His condition gradually improved. At that time, his appetite also increased. All the doctors believed that life had some hope. Shigemitsu's brother and younger brother also showed a slight relief. The most dangerous time was 2 p.m. yesterday, when his body temperature was still 40 degrees Celsius, his pulse reached 130, and his breathing was 29. Medical Doctor Goto also shook his head. After 6 p.m. last night, Goto told people that Shigemitsu's life could be saved.

Hospital Announcement: Last night, according to the announcement from Fumin Hospital, Minister Shigemitsu's condition was as follows: At 3 a.m. yesterday, his body temperature was 37.7 degrees Celsius, his pulse was 90, and his breathing was 26. At 5 a.m., it was 38.6 degrees Celsius, his pulse was 106, and his breathing was 26. At 11 a.m., it was 40 degrees Celsius, his pulse was 118, and his breathing was 26. At 2 p.m., it was 40 degrees Celsius, his pulse was 130, and his breathing was 29. At 6 p.m., it was 38.2 degrees Celsius, his pulse was 108, and his breathing was 26.

Ambassadors Visit: British Ambassador Lampson visited Shigemitsu at Fumin Hospital at 11:20 a.m. yesterday, and American Ambassador Johnson visited him at 2:30 p.m. yesterday to express his condolences. Medical Doctor Goto described his condition in detail to both ambassadors.

Nomura Recovering: Nomura's injury has been recovering yesterday. His body temperature was 36.6 degrees Celsius, his pulse was 76, and his appetite increased. The shrapnel in his waist was removed yesterday. There were no changes in Shirakawa and Ueda.

The Municipal Public Safety Bureau Prepares to Take Over Police Authority in War Zone 91

Survey of Destroyed Police Stations Completed

Only Three of More Than Ten Stations are Intact

The Municipal Public Safety Bureau, led by Wen Yingxing, has held several meetings with its staff to discuss the takeover of police authority in the Zhabei and Wusong areas. A committee of eight members has been appointed to prepare for all takeover matters. Wen also sent personnel to survey the destroyed police stations and substations in the war zone. Repairs are now underway so that they can be restored to their original condition after the Japanese troops withdraw. The list of members of the Police Authority Takeover Committee and the details of the destroyed and intact police stations in the war zone are listed below:

Takeover Committee Members: Section Chief of the 1st Section, Zhen Shaoshen; Section Chief of the 2nd Section, Wang Zhijing; Section Chief of the 3rd Section, Wu Zhiquan; Secretary, Feng Shuluan; Ju Jing; Chief Inspector, Gong Xikui; Police Battalion Commander, Huang Zhao; Detective Squad Leader, Lu Ying.

Destroyed Police Stations: Baoshan Road 5th District Headquarters; Baziqiao Substation; Yipin Lane Substation; Qiujiang Road 5th District 2nd Substation and police outposts; Hujiamuqiao 5th District 3rd Substation; Yinxianggang 5th District 4th Substation; Jiangwan 5th District 5th Substation; Wusong 7th District Headquarters; also 7th District 3rd Substation, all substations, and all police outposts were destroyed by Japanese artillery fire or bombing, leaving only ruins.

Intact Police Stations: Qiujiang Road 5th District 1st Substation; Changan Road 4th District 1st Substation; Zhenru 4th District 3rd Substation. Although the above three locations were not destroyed by Japanese artillery fire or bombing, all the furniture and supplies inside were completely destroyed by the Japanese troops.

Repairs Underway: As the peace agreement has been officially signed, the Municipal Public Safety Bureau, led by Wen Yingxing, has started the retreat of Japanese troops from the Zhabei and Wusong areas. The public safety of the area urgently needs police to maintain order. However, as most of the police stations have been destroyed by Japanese fire, personnel have been dispatched to Wusong, Zhabei, and Zhenru to quickly repair the damaged police stations so that police can be sent to maintain order as soon as the Japanese troops withdraw.

Various Groups Oppose: The Shanghai Federation of All Groups held its 42nd standing committee meeting yesterday at 4 PM, chaired by Yin Zhiling and recorded by Wu Yixin. The discussion concerned the National Government's declaration of tolerance for the organization of special police and the hiring of experts as police officers and instructors, which is clearly surrendering sovereignty and humiliating the country. The meeting resolved to send a telegram of opposition and appointed Li Cishan to draft it.

Changes in Defense of Suzhou Creek 93

U.S. Troops Hand Over Duties to Police

Japanese Troops Cross Border, Ready to Protest

Continental News reports that the area south of Suzhou Creek in the Public Concession, previously defended by British and American troops rotating every three months, will be handed over to the police starting today as the situation eases. The defense of the area was previously rotated between British and American troops every fifteen days. Recently, the Defense Committee of the Concession decided to gradually return border defense to the police as the situation in Shanghai has eased. The current U.S. troops are scheduled to complete their term of duty today and will hand over duties to the police without being replaced by British troops. It is claimed that the handover of defense duties by the U.S. troops was decided earlier and has absolutely no connection with the incident on Tuesday when Japanese soldiers entered the territory and injured Chinese citizens, or the subsequent standoff between U.S. and Japanese troops. Regarding the incident on Tuesday, a U.S. military officer stated yesterday that they consider the case closed and that relations between the U.S. and Japanese troops are completely harmonious. Officials of the Municipal Council stated that there is an understanding among the troops of various countries cooperating in the defense of the Public Concession that they will not cross borders and infringe on rights. If the Japanese troops have any complaints about residents within the U.S. defense area, they should negotiate with the U.S. authorities and not take action on their own. The Japanese troops' intrusion into the U.S. defense area and unauthorized actions violated the understanding. The U.S. troops stopped them themselves. The incident was raised for discussion at yesterday's regular meeting of the Municipal Council directors. It is expected that after the police submit a final detailed report, the Municipal Council will lodge a protest.

Plans to Reopen the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway 94

Service to Resume Immediately After Japanese Troops Withdraw

Mr. Zheng Baozhao, Chief of the Traffic Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways Administration, told reporters from the National News Agency yesterday that since the outbreak of the Shanghai war, the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway has been shortened, and many tracks and bridges east of Kunshan have been destroyed. Now that the ceasefire agreement has been signed, the administration will begin implementing preliminary plans, including: (1) repairing railway tracks and bridges; (2) quickly building temporary office spaces at the destroyed stations; (3) repairing and replenishing traffic signals, electrical road signs, traffic telegrams, telephones, electric lights, and other traffic-related equipment; (4) coordinating vehicles and setting temporary train schedules; (5) making every effort to provide various conveniences for passengers within the possible scope; (6) printing various passenger tickets. In addition to the above six items, the Qingyang Port Bridge must also be repaired as soon as possible. Before the repairs are completed, if the Japanese troops have already withdrawn, a pontoon bridge will be built first, and three locomotives and twenty passenger cars will be borrowed from the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway to transport passengers to Qingyang Port for transfer. The railway bureau will be responsible for transferring luggage and goods. However, the work will be completed in two to three days at most. The date of resuming service cannot be determined yet, as it is not known when the Japanese troops will withdraw.

Respectfully, to the General Office of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council.

Relief for Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry 96

Establishment of Two Committees

Suspension of Raw Silk Tax and Public Bond Surcharge

Subsidy of 100 Taels Per Load for Exported Raw Silk

The silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has been in decline for years, reaching a critical point. The Shanghai Incident has had a particularly significant impact. For example, less than one-tenth of the 113 single and double palace silk mills in Shanghai are barely surviving. The spring cocoon season is approaching, but few silk merchants are organizing to collect cocoons. The governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, for the sake of the livelihoods of farmers, have requested the National Government for relief. The government has now appointed special commissioners and established the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Aged Silk and Cocoon Sorting Committee and the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Stored Silk Sales Committee, which will officially begin operations today. The details are listed below:

Relief Measures: Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Department of Industry of Zhejiang Province, and He Yushu, Director of the Department of Industry of Jiangsu Province, went to Nanjing to negotiate with the relevant authorities on the relief of the silk and cocoon industry. Tan Zhongkui, Director of the Agricultural and Forestry Department, Zhang Fuyun, Director of the State Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance, and the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces consulted on relief measures. As a result, the governments of the two provinces invited representatives of the banking industry, silk merchants, and silkworm farmers of the two provinces to hold a meeting at the Bank of China in Shanghai to discuss relief measures. The following resolutions were made: (1) The governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces will find ways to raise funds for relief. (2) The export tax on raw silk will be suspended to encourage exports. (3) The surcharge for the silk industry public bond fund will be suspended to reduce the burden. (4) The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Aged Silk and Cocoon Sorting Committee will be established. (5) The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Stored Silk Sales Committee will be established. (6) A plan for the fundamental relief of the raw silk industry in the future will be developed. (7) A plan for the collection of cocoons this spring will be developed.

Appointment of Committee Members: Yesterday, the government issued an official order appointing the members of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Aged Silk and Cocoon Sorting Committee as Xu Boming, Shen Xiqing, Cai Wuji, Li Zufa, Qin Runqing, Feng Zhongqing, Huo Baoshu, Ye Zhuotang, Zhu Jing'an, Shen Huachen, Qian Fenghao, Sheng Lianxin, and others, thirteen in total. The members of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Stored Silk Sales Committee are Xie Zuokai, He Bingxian, Wang Zhixin, Chen Julin, Xie Taofu, Bei Songsun, Li Shoushan, Wu Shenbo, Xue Shouquan, Zhou Junmei, Li Shuchu, Presi and Fumegali, thirteen in total.

Official Establishment: Yesterday, the two committees held a meeting at the Bank of China and elected Xu Boming, Cai Wuji, Li Zufa, Qin Runqing, Huo Baoshu, Ye Zhuotang, and Zhu Jing'an as standing committee members of the Zhejiang Aged Silk and Cocoon Committee, and Xie Zuokai, He Bingxian, Chen Julin, Xie Taofu, Bei Songsun, Wu Shenbo, and Li Shuchu as standing committee members of the Stored Silk Sales Committee. The committees were officially established, and an office was set up on the third floor of No. 15 Museum Road, which will begin operations immediately from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM.

Notice to All Sectors: The first notice of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Aged Silk and Cocoon Sorting Committee states: It has been found that the amount of aged silk and cocoons accumulated in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces over the years is very large, and the impact is worrying. The governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, in view of this, have allocated funds for relief. All aged silk and cocoons in the two provinces, as well as factory silk reeled from aged cocoons, will be subsidized with 100 taels of silver per load when exported overseas (no subsidies will be given for those not exported). At the same time, the two provincial governments have submitted a request to the National Government and sent a notice to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry to suspend the collection of raw silk export tax and the silk industry public bond fund surcharge to reduce the burden. The committee has been established to handle the sorting procedures. All aged silk and cocoons that have been mortgaged must be registered with the committee by May 15th (May 20th for other ports). (The government will no longer provide subsidies for those who fail to register by the deadline.) The committee will then send personnel to inspect and weigh the goods and issue certificates to prevent confusion and avoid missing out. The deadline is approaching, so please do not delay and miss the opportunity. This notice is hereby given.

Reasons for Consolidating the Postal Foundation: Specific Proposals 100

Presented by the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union (Continued)

Reason Two: The reason why postal savings are most secure is that the personnel managing the savings are postal workers, whose appointments and benefits are guaranteed, allowing them to serve with peace of mind, be honest and impartial, and because the post office serves as a guarantor, it gains the trust of the public. Since the establishment of a special bureau for savings and remittance, the people employed have not been limited to postal personnel. Recently, due to political changes, the bureau chiefs have been replaced accordingly, and as a result, dozens of personnel in the general bureau and its affiliated branch bureaus have also been replaced. Previously, the general bureau employed postal personnel and external personnel in a ratio of about half and half. Now, postal personnel are being sent back to the post office to serve, and it seems that savings and remittances will all be managed by people unrelated to the post office, while still using the name "Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau". It is unfair to make the post office and its personnel bear the responsibility. Moreover, although the total amount of postal savings is now 30 million yuan, and the amount of remittances is 200 million yuan, each item is extremely trivial and consists of the hard-earned money of ordinary people. The trivial amounts result in increasingly complex accounting records. If the responsible persons are not in their positions for a long time, problems will arise, and there will be no way to investigate. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau has only been established for two years, and the phenomenon of personnel changes following politics has already been discovered. In the future, if political officials change frequently, the bureau's personnel will also change accordingly. The more frequent the changes, the more confused the responsibilities will be, and the hard-earned money of ordinary people will definitely be in danger. For the sake of the interests of the people and the credit of the post office, the postal savings and remittance business should be returned to the post office. This is one reason. According to Article 33 of the International Postal Convention, "Other agencies may join the exchange of bills of exchange. If the remittance business of various countries is handled by agencies other than the post office, they may also join the bill of exchange procedures stipulated in the various articles of this agreement." The agency handling the bill of exchange business must consult with the post office of its own country on everything in order to implement it. All provisions of this agreement, all exchanges between the agency and other countries joining this agreement and the International Postal Bureau, shall be relayed by the post office of its own country. Now that the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau is gradually sending postal personnel back to the post office, in the future, the international community may recognize the bureau as a non-postal agency and request the separate formulation of a gold remittance bureau. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau is gradually sending postal personnel back to the post office, and in the future, the international community may recognize the bureau as a non-postal agency and request the separate formulation of an exchange bill system. The position of our country's post office in the international community will be greatly affected. This is the second reason. "The name 'Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau' implies that it is an agency for handling postal savings and remittance business, but in reality, postal personnel will soon disappear from it." This is not debatable. The backbone of the general bureau consists of three businesses: savings, remittance, and insurance. Now, the postal personnel who were sent to Japan to study insurance matters with dedication have been returned to the post office to serve, and the deputy director of the savings department who has many years of experience in handling postal savings has also been sent back to the post office. Furthermore, the director of the department has been transferred to another position, and the director of the remittance department has been appointed to concurrently manage the savings department. The deputy director of the remittance department has also been dismissed. Originally, four people were in charge of the two departments, but now one person is in charge of everything. It is speculated that the intention is to save money. However, the simplification of the general bureau's backbone business has been proven by facts. The affairs of the three departments of savings, remittance, and insurance, which are the backbone businesses, can be handled so easily. Then, the general bureau can be renamed the "Postal Funds Management Bureau" and the words "Savings and Remittance" can be removed. Wouldn't that be a name that matches reality? If the intention is to save money, then why not merge the bureau into the Postal General Bureau and return to the original organization? Wouldn't that be even more economical? Moreover, the facts should be like this. The affairs handled by the general bureau have been handled by the Postal General Bureau for 30 years with only a department established, and its business has indeed been developing year by year. Now, a separate general bureau has been established, creating an unnecessary position of bureau chief, two deputy bureau chiefs, and heads of the general affairs office, the secretary's office, the accounting office, the joint accounting office, the insurance office (still in preparation for handling simple insurance business), deputy heads, secretaries, consultants, medical officers, section chiefs, clerks, office assistants, assistants, trainees, and other committee members, totaling one or two hundred people. Their salaries, pensions, rents, and office expenses amount to a total waste of 1.5 to 1.6 million yuan per year, which is borne by the post office. If it is said that this expenditure can be offset by the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau making banking business outside of the savings and remittance business, earning income, I would like to ask whether the bureau has a special fund for its establishment and whether the established credit is fully utilized by using the post office's working capital and credit to engage in the banking business. To discuss in detail, the bureau was established by taking the Japanese charter as a model. According to Japanese law, the Postal Savings Bureau should not engage in banking business and compete with other banks. Even if the country allows it to concurrently operate this business, can't the Postal General Bureau also concurrently operate it? Why set up a special bureau to manage the funds? Moreover, the current director of the bureau, Yang Jianping, is skilled in military logistics and is not a banking expert. Can he be better than the personnel of the Postal General Bureau? If it is said that a special bureau must be established to specialize in responsibilities and promote development, then a dedicated deputy director can be placed under the director of the Postal General Bureau to handle the affairs with ease. Why create such unnecessary expenses? Japan established a separate Postal Savings Bureau only more than 20 years ago. At that time, Japan's small country savings had reached 300 million Japanese yen, so it felt that the affairs had become increasingly complex, and there was a split. Now, our country's savings are less than 30 million silver yuan, and there is absolutely no need to split. This is the third reason. In addition to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, the separate establishment of savings and remittance branch bureaus in Nanjing and Hankou is not allowed by the systems of other countries, nor is it allowed by the Japanese system that is being taken as a model. The waste is even greater, and it is absolutely a redundant agency. This is the fourth reason. Currently, the Postal General Bureau and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau have joint presentations to the Ministry of Communications, and the Postal Department has joint letters, and there are joint orders, joint circulars, joint announcements, and joint telegrams to the postal directors and personnel of various regions. This is unprecedented in other countries. There are official documents and letters for mutual consultation on official matters. The procedures are cumbersome and time-consuming, which is extremely inconvenient. Previously, the appointment, reward, punishment, and promotion of postal personnel were carried out by the director of the Postal General Bureau in accordance with regulations, and the authority was unified. Now, important vacancies and matters involving savings and remittance affairs are handled by the Postal General Bureau after soliciting the consent of the Savings and Remittance Bureau. The Savings and Remittance Bureau can appoint outsiders as managers, directors, section chiefs, etc. without the consent of the Postal General Bureau. This is putting the cart before the horse, and there are two separate branches. This is truly an unprecedented example in ancient and modern times, both at home and abroad. The Postal General Bureau cannot manage all the funds of the post office. In case of emergency needs, it must take out interest and overdraft from the Savings and Remittance Bureau, which is also unreasonable. If this continues for a long time, it is feared that the postal personnel will become increasingly resentful and will not be able to cooperate with the Savings and Remittance Bureau. Therefore, a merger should be urgently carried out. This is the fifth reason. Based on the above five points, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau should be merged into the Postal General Bureau. For the convenience of the transition, the director of the Postal General Bureau should temporarily take over the Postal General Bureau. The future organization must be handled in accordance with the proposals in March, April, May, and July. The reason is nothing more than to protect the hard-earned money of the people, managed by guaranteed personnel, not affected by political trends, and able to specialize in their responsibilities and promote their development, which is not only to save 1.5 to 1.6 million yuan in unnecessary expenses and reduce the burden on the post office.

Reason Three: Airmail is originally a new business in modern times, and the state should run it to meet the needs of business. However, no country that runs airmail has not lost money. Taking the United States, the most developed country in airmail, as an example, the annual loss is nearly 9 million US dollars, which is equivalent to about 40 million Chinese currency. Our country's post office is just beginning to sprout, how can it bear this burden? Moreover, there is a need to open up postal routes in remote areas to promote culture everywhere. How can we rush to decorate the facade? If the government is determined to run it, it should also allocate funds from the national treasury. Otherwise, the Ministry of Communications will allocate the 1.3 million yuan that the post office has remitted over the years (from the 18th to the 20th year). (See the above). In addition to paying the mail freight, the company should also be responsible for all the expenses of the company, which amount to tens of thousands of yuan a year, thereby hindering the development of the post office. Therefore, the airline should be run by the government with funds allocated, and at the same time, the post office should no longer bear any subsidies for aviation, and its remaining strength should be used to fully develop the post office itself and gradually seek its development. The post office and aviation can then advance together without limits.

Reason Four: The post office's budget for this year is actually 4 million yuan short. Now that the national treasury is exhausted, it is difficult to seek government assistance to make up for the post office's losses. Therefore, the only way is to first find the source of the post office's losses and make overall plans for specific plans to consolidate the postal foundation. For example, the principle of "supporting the post office with the post office" as stated in the above reasons, the abolition of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, and the cessation of all subsidies to aviation companies must be actively promoted to be implemented. At least, more than 4 million yuan in unnecessary expenses can be saved annually. Although the current shortage urgently needs to be opened up to supplement the source of funds, this is only a temporary transitional difficulty and is not the root cause of the post office's problems. If the temporary difficulties are used to increase postage rates by as much as 50% without regard to the future of the post office and the burdens on the people, and no fundamental improvements are made in postal administration, it will only increase the burdens on the public, and the result of the increase will not help the current post office at all. Moreover, according to the rates set by the Ministry, the post office's revenue can be increased by more than 10 million yuan annually. However, if the post office can earnestly implement the principle of "supporting the post office with the post office" and save all unnecessary and excessive expenses of agencies, the natural surplus each year will be at least more than 2 million yuan. Combined, the post office can expect to have a surplus of more than 10 million yuan annually, excluding legitimate expenses and development costs. It is doubtful whether the post office, which acts as a labor agent, needs such a large surplus. The Ministry's hard work in maintaining the post office is greatly appreciated. However, what the union and others dare not agree with is that the Ministry does not first write a plan to consolidate the postal foundation and the post office's minimum budget, and then seek ways to adjust the postal economy to solve the current difficulties, so that the people can understand the truth of the postal economy and understand the reasons for the post office's losses. They all admire the Ministry's hard work in maintaining the post office and are happy to bear the burden. The government can also avoid attacks from public opinion, which is truly a manifestation of the spirit of governance. This is why the union and others advocate maintaining the original postage rates temporarily and requesting the Ministry to first plan for fundamental plans. (End)

Wu Mai's Case Against Wu Tiecheng and Others Transferred Jurisdiction 107

Under the Jurisdiction of Jiangning District Court

Wu Mai's lawsuit against Wu Tiecheng and others for injury and confinement in the Shanghai District Court has been reported in various newspapers. This case has been ordered by the Jiangsu High Court to transfer jurisdiction to the Jiangning District Court. The text of the High Court's ruling is recorded as follows: Jiangsu High Court Criminal Ruling 20th Year Sheng Zi No. 282. Ruling applicant: Prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court. The right applicant requested a transfer of jurisdiction due to Wu Mai's obstruction of official duties, incitement to escape, and Wu Tiecheng and others' injury and dereliction of duty. The court ruled as follows: Main text: This case should be transferred to the Jiangning District Court for first-instance jurisdiction. Reason: The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau reported to the prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court that Wu Mai obstructed official duties and incited escape, and that Wu Mai accused Wu Tiecheng and others of injury and dereliction of duty. According to the prosecutor's application, this case arose because Wu Mai, representing the Shanghai Municipal Middle School Federation, failed to bail out communist suspects from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. Wu Mai is also a person who has been wanted. After reviewing the case files investigated by this office, the facts are clear. Since this office accepted this case, letters and notes of concern from groups such as the Republic of China National Salvation Association, the Southeast Five Provinces Anti-Japanese Association, and the National Lawyers Association have been sent one after another. Wu Mai is also comparable to someone with a considerable reputation in Shanghai society. Others, such as Wu Tiecheng, are the highest administrative officials of Shanghai and are currently also important officials in the country dealing with foreign affairs. Wen Yingxing, Wu Zhiquan, and others are police officers directly maintaining public security in Shanghai. At this time, a violent neighbor is invading the country, and Shanghai is an important area for war. In this environment, accepting this case, whether the defendant is guilty or innocent in the future, will inevitably harm public security. The application for transfer of jurisdiction is consistent with the provisions of Article 21, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law and should be approved to transfer this case to the Jiangning District Court for first-instance jurisdiction. This ruling is made as the main text. April 25, 21st Year of the Republic of China. Jiangsu High Court Criminal Third Tribunal Judge and Presiding Judge Song Yuan, Judge Zheng Zhiguo, Judge Yin Yuxu. It is certified that the original is consistent with the original. Jiangsu High Court Clerk Ma Yiqing, April 28, 21st Year of the Republic of China.

The Municipal Party Department Is Willing to Lead to Achieve the Purpose of Rent Reduction and Exemption

The Municipal Government Has Ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to Provide Detailed Measures

Since the Shanghai Citizens' Rent Reduction and Exemption Committee formulated the rent reduction and exemption measures by district, and submitted them to the general meeting for approval and promulgation, few landlords have expressed acceptance, and most are still waiting and watching. Bullets Flew on Beil Road; Detective and Thief Died 109

One of the Three Bandits Was Captured

A Stray Bullet Injured a Passerby

At 8:30 last night, a gunfight between a detective and bandits occurred on Beil Road, Route Cardinal Foch, in the French Concession. Jin Baoyi, a newly promoted detective, was shot in the head by a bandit and died on the spot. A stray bullet injured a pedestrian. As a result, one bandit was captured. The details are recorded as follows:

After the Ma Case Occurred: After the major case in which Yifa, the fifth son of Ma Changsheng, a major antique merchant on Route Grolier, was kidnapped and the chauffeur Xia Baosheng was shot dead on the spot, the police authorities of the French Concession attached great importance to it and ordered all subordinates to investigate strictly in order to solve the case in the shortest possible time. As a result, the detectives of each police station felt more stressed, and the uniformed detectives who checked pedestrians on the road felt even more responsible.

Three Suspicious Youths: At about 6:00 last night, Uniformed Detective Lu Zhulin, along with Detective Zhao Chunsheng and newly promoted Detective Jin Baoyi, were checking pedestrians at various important road junctions. At 8:30, when they were checking east to west at the corner of Beil Road and Route Cardinal Foch at the Eight Immortals Bridge, three youths dressed in blue cloth shorts suddenly walked towards them, and their appearance was very suspicious. The detectives ordered them to stop, but not only did the three not stop, but they turned around and ran away, and fired a shot to demonstrate.

Detective Shot Dead: Seeing that the situation was not good, the detectives also drew their guns and chased after them. The two sides fired at each other more than 20 shots. Detective Jin was shot twice, one bullet hitting his right temple and penetrating his brain, and he fell to the ground and died immediately. Two of the bandits fled north into the International Settlement and disappeared in an instant. One bandit dressed in blue cloth shorts fled south to the front of the National Western Clothing Store at No. 242 Avenue Joffre and was intercepted by Chinese Constables from No. 65 who were stationed there, along with Detective Zhao. A Mauser pistol and more than ten bullets were seized on the spot.

Stray Bullet Injures One Person: After one bandit was captured, the police station heard the alarm and dispatched a large number of detectives to help capture the bandits. However, the remaining bandits had long since disappeared. They immediately transported the body of Detective Jin to the Tongren Fu Yuan Funeral Home to wait for an autopsy. At the same time, they took the captured bandit into the police station. According to the bandit, he was from Anhui, but his age and name were temporarily not disclosed. When the detectives and bandits were firing at each other, bullets flew on Beil Road, and a stray bullet injured Zhou Yuehu, a pedestrian. It was found that Zhou was from Taicang, 33 years old, and worked as a tailor. He is currently a partner at Wang Shunxing Tailor Shop at No. 22 Daohaili, Beil Road. The bullet hit his left thigh and he went to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Preferential Treatment to Comfort the Loyal Soul: Afterwards, it was learned that Detective Jin Baoyi was originally from Siyang, only 36 years old, and had served as Chinese Constable No. 362 in the French Concession for many years. Because of his loyalty and bravery, he had repeatedly won merits and was recently promoted to probationary detective No. 61. He had only been married for a short time, and now he died in the line of duty. Those who heard about it regretted it. It is said that the police station authorities intend to give him the most preferential treatment in order to comfort his loyal soul and show future generations.

Westerner Opens Large Casino in the French Concession 111

A Westerner, Harry Mees (transliteration), 38 years old and a Czech national, recently set up a roulette casino on the second floor of No. 341 Avenue Meyers, French Concession. Li Daiyi, the Western Chief Detective of the French police, learned of his drawing profits from gambling and on the evening of the 4th, led Chinese detectives He Tugeng and Liu Kunbao, along with detectives on duty, to the premises. There they arrested Harry Mees and nine gamblers: Lin Weitian, Lin Zhangshi, Lin Sanmei, Li Qi, Li Wangshi (all from Fujian), Zhu Miaofeng, Wang Gengsheng (both local), and Bao Fucheng (from Suzhou), men and women in total. They seized gambling paraphernalia including one roulette wheel, two pieces of table cloth, three ivory chips, twelve boxes of chips, one small suitcase, nine hard paper gambling cards, eleven account books, and gambling money totaling 194 silver dollars. In a room on the third floor, they also discovered one set of smoking paraphernalia and a lamp gun, along with parts. The suspects were taken to the police station. After interrogation by the police chief, the gamblers were each ordered to pay 30 silver dollars in cash for bail while Harry Mees was detained. Yesterday, they were escorted to the Fourth Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court to be tried by Judge Wu Fanglian. First, Gu Shouxi, the police lawyer, explained the case, stating that the defendant had privately established a gambling den, gathered people to gamble, and profited from it, violating Article 280 of the Criminal Law, and requested that he be investigated and prosecuted according to the law. Next, the officer in charge, Bao, reported the details of the arrest and presented the evidence. The bailed-out gamblers had not appeared in court. When questioned, the defendant Harry Mees confessed that he was hired by a certain Wang to manage the casino, which had started operating on the evening of the 3rd. He claimed not to know Wang's whereabouts and denied any knowledge of the smoking paraphernalia found. After examining the confession, the court ordered the defendant to pay a security deposit of one thousand dollars and provide a guarantor; without a guarantor, he would be detained. The case was adjourned for further hearing.

Da Xin Silk and Satin Bureau Submits Document to the Ministry of Industry 113

The Da Xin Silk and Satin Bureau, located at the intersection of Shilu and Sanma Road, has recently observed the slow sales of domestic silk and satin. In addition to launching a large-scale clearance sale starting from May 5th to promote sales, the bureau also advocates promoting silk clothing in the hope of achieving significant results. The bureau has specially submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry to establish regulations and issue a national mandate for uniform compliance. The original submission is excerpted below: The submission is for requesting prompt issuance of regulations to promote silk clothing, in order to encourage and enrich the people's livelihood. It is believed that today our country is subjected to the invasion of the violent Japanese externally, and internally feels the decline of people's livelihood. Dangerous situations arise in cycles, and the danger of subjugation is worrying. Therefore, the way to save the country and enrich the people's livelihood cannot be delayed. Our bureau adheres to the principle of saving the country through our own industry, and thus has a modest proposal to promote silk clothing, which is presented herewith. Silk is a unique national treasure of our country, shining upon the world for thousands of years and a major part of international trade. Today, it is declining and dying, resulting in farmers not daring to plant mulberry trees, village women not daring to raise silkworms, workers not reeling silk, and merchants not trading it. All are afraid of the slow sales of silk. Its direct and indirect impact on the people's livelihood is enormous. Our bureau has identified the crux of the problem, and therefore believes that to promote domestic goods, one must start with the silk industry, and to promote silk, one must promote silk clothing to expand its sales. This is not only a good remedy for rescuing the silk industry but also a superior strategy for enriching the people's livelihood. Ever since the popularity of Western suits, foreign wool and broadcloth have flooded the market, causing a painful blow to the sales of silk clothing materials. However, the value of wool and broadcloth has never been cheaper than silk. It can be seen that the slow sales of silk are not due to the people's weak purchasing power, but to the popularity of Western suits and the flooding of wool and broadcloth. If the government authorities can now establish regulations to promote silk clothing and issue a national mandate for uniform compliance, the effect of superiors leading by example will be enormous. Considering that Japanese women are required to wear kimonos when attending aristocratic banquets to emphasize their national identity, which has profound significance for preserving their national essence. China's industry is nascent, and the people's wisdom is not yet widespread, and relies on the government to promote and guide it, so as to provide support. Our bureau, within the limits of our humble knowledge, dares to submit this request to your esteemed ministry for review and approval, to allow the establishment of regulations to promote silk clothing, in order to encourage and enrich the people's livelihood. In a state of urgent expectation, we respectfully await your orders and submit this to the Ministry of Industry.

Criminals Swap Identities, Openly Serve Sentences for Each Other 115

Heavier Penalties Imposed After Discovery

Court Now Photographing All Criminals

The robber Xu Aqin was sentenced to twelve years in prison by the Shanghai District Court. While the case was being finalized, the opium offender Wang Xuesheng was sentenced to fifty days of detention. When they were jointly sent to the Second Prison in Caohejing, Xu Aqin and Wang Xuesheng conspired to exchange names, so that Xu Aqin was executed as Wang Xuesheng, and Wang Xuesheng was executed as Xu Aqin. However, Wang Xuesheng's sentence was very short, so he was released according to law after a short period. Thus, Xu Aqin escaped the law by impersonating Wang Xuesheng. But Wang Xuesheng, having impersonated Xu Aqin, should have served a twelve-year sentence on his behalf. However, his plan was cunning: if he explained the matter afterwards, there would be no legal basis for serving a sentence on behalf of another person, and at most he would be given additional punishment, but not the long term of twelve years. Therefore, as soon as Xu Aqin was released under the false name, Wang Xuesheng immediately declared the error. The prison staff immediately reported to Warden Dong, and Wang Xuesheng was sent to the District Court for interrogation. At the same time, a large reward was offered for the capture of Xu Aqin, who was captured in the countryside of Chuansha and also sent to the court. The two criminals Wang and Xu have been given heavier penalties. However, cases of criminals swapping identities have become increasingly common recently. Therefore, the court now plans to photograph all convicted criminals and include the photographs with the case files for execution.
